Interpreting 'Hatta' in Oaths: Literal Meaning and Custom
Explaining literal and customary interpretation of hatta in oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that the literal meaning of 'hatta' as a goal is presumed unless custom makes it impossible, in which case custom defines the limit, and derive the ruling on oath-breaking.

Core Idea
Hatta in oaths is literal; but if literal is impossible, custom determines the limit.

In this lesson, we examine how the particle 'hatta' (until) is interpreted in oaths. The starting point is its literal meaning as a goal (ghaya), but when literal application is impossible due to custom, custom overrides. This principle is illustrated by two scenarios from Usul al-Shashi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the oath statement and the particle 'hatta'
Look for the phrase structure: '[action] until [goal]'. The particle 'hatta' indicates the intended limit.
2
Check if the goal is achievable as a literal limit
Determine whether the goal can actually be the endpoint of the action. For example, paying a debt can be the endpoint of separation.
If the goal is possible, literal meaning applies.
3
If the literal goal is impossible, consult custom
When the literal meaning cannot be applied (e.g., beating until death is not a realistic limit), custom ('urf) replaces the literal interpretation.
Custom defines a reasonable limit (e.g., severe beating).
4
Apply the determined interpretation
If literal, the oath is broken if the goal is not reached. If custom, the limit set by custom applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل حتّى للغاية

الحالف: يغارق غريمه حتى يقضيه دينه ففارقه قبل قضاء الدين حنث. فإذا تعذر العمل بالحقيقة لمانع كالعرف، كما لو حلف أن يضربه حتى يموت أو حتى يقتله، حمل على الضرب الشديد باعتبار العرف، وإن لم يكن الأول قابلاً للامتداد والآخر صالحاً للغاية وصلح الأول سبباً والآخر جزاء يحمل على الجزاء، ويترك حقيقته وهي الغاية. مثاله ما قال محمد رحمه الله: إذا قال لغيره: «عبدي حر إن لم آتك حتى تغديني» فأتاه فلم يغده لا يحنث؛ لأن التغدية لا تصلح غاية للإتيان بل هي داع إلى زيادة الإتيان وصلحت جزاء فيحمل على الجزاء فيكون بمعنى لام كي.
Chapter: Hatta for Ghaya. The one swearing: He separates from his debtor until he pays his debt, so if he separates before paying the debt, he breaks his oath. If acting upon the literal meaning is impossible due to a preventer such as custom, as if he swore to beat him until he dies or until he kills him, it is interpreted as severe beating based on custom. And if the first [action] is not capable of extension and the second is suitable as a goal, and the first is valid as a cause and the second as a result, it is interpreted as a result, and its literal meaning (ghaya) is abandoned. Example: What Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said: If someone says to another: 'My slave is free if I do not come to you until you feed me,' then he comes but he does not feed him, he does not break the oath because feeding is not suitable as a goal for coming; rather it is an incentive for increased coming and is valid as a result, so it is interpreted as a result, meaning the lam of kai.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This is a textual analysis from Usul al-Shashi focusing on how the particle 'hatta' (حتى) is interpreted in oaths. The text presents three scenarios: (1) When 'hatta' literally indicates a goal that is possible, it is taken literally; breaking the oath occurs if the limit is not reached. (2) When literal interpretation is impossible, custom overrides, e.g., beating until death is interpreted as severe beating. (3) When the first verb does not extend to the goal and the second is a suitable result or compensation, 'hatta' is interpreted as a causal particle (like lam of kai), indicating that the second action is the purpose of the first. The example from Imam Muhammad illustrates the third case: feeding cannot be a goal of coming, so it is treated as a reward or result; if he comes but is not fed, the oath is not violated.

Key Terms
حتى (hatta): A particle that can indicate the goal (ghaya) of an action or, in some contexts, the result (jaza).
الغاية (al-ghaya): The ultimate limit or goal of an action.
الجزاء (al-jaza): The result or compensation that is the purpose of the action, not the limit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the default interpretation of 'hatta' in an oath?
A) It indicates a causal purpose (jaza).
B) It indicates a literal goal (ghaya) unless custom or impossibility prevents it.
C) It always follows the most common custom.
D) It is interpreted as a metaphorical expression.

Key Takeaway
The literal meaning of 'hatta' as a goal is the default; custom overrides only when literal is impossible.

8 min
When 'Hatta' Indicates a Result (Jaza) in Oaths
Explaining the causal interpretation of hatta when the first action is not extendable

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recognize when the particle 'hatta' in an oath should be interpreted as indicating a result (jaza) rather than a goal, and apply the Hanafi rule that the causative meaning (lam of kai) is intended.

Core Idea
When the first action cannot extend to the goal, 'hatta' shifts from limit to purpose: the result is the real intent.

This lesson explores a special case where 'hatta' cannot be taken as a literal goal because the first action (such as coming) does not admit of extension to the second (feeding). Instead, 'hatta' is interpreted as a causal particle (like lam al-ta'lil), indicating that the second action is the purpose of the first. The example from Imam Muhammad illustrates this.

Guided Path
1
Identify that the first action is not extendable to a limit
Some actions, like 'coming', are punctual and cannot be continued until another action occurs. Recognize this type of verb.
2
Examine the second action: is it a suitable result or compensation?
The second action should be something that can be the purpose of the first action, not a natural limit. For example, feeding can be the result of coming (you come to be fed).
3
Determine that 'hatta' indicates the cause and result relationship
Since the first action cannot be extended to the second, 'hatta' is reinterpreted as carrying the meaning of 'lam al-kai' (in order that). The first action is a cause, the second is a result.
4
Apply this to the example from Imam Muhammad
In 'until you feed me', feeding is not a limit of coming; it is the purpose. Therefore, if he comes but is not fed, the condition 'until you feed me' is not violated because the feeding is not a requirement for the oath; only the cause (coming) matters.

The Meaning of 'Ala' for Obligation and Its Application in Aman
Explaining the word 'ala' as indicating obligation and its usage in aman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the preposition 'ala' as a term indicating obligation in Hanafi usul, distinguish its legal effect from words like 'indee', and apply this rule to determine who has the right to designate individuals in an aman contract.

Core Idea
The word 'ala' imposes superiority and obligation: whoever says 'ala' over a debt or right becomes bound, whereas 'indee' merely states possession.

A single preposition can determine legal obligations. The Hanafi usul tradition gives specific weight to the word 'ala' (على) as a marker of obligation (ilzam), derived from its literal meaning of elevation. This lesson unpacks the linguistic basis and then shows how this principle plays out in the practical context of aman (safe-conduct) during war, where the choice of whom to protect hinges on the wording used.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its linguistic origin
Recognize 'ala' as a preposition with a literal meaning of superiority/elevation. This is the basis for its legal usage.
The text cites physical examples like 'Zaid is on the roof' and abstract like 'he is over us as an amir'.
2
Distinguish legal usage from similar words
When 'ala' is used in obligation contexts (e.g., 'alayya dayn'), it indicates a debt owed. In contrast, 'indee', 'ma'ee', 'qablee' indicate mere possession without obligation.
This distinction is critical for understanding when a statement creates a binding duty.
3
Apply the rule to the aman scenario
If the chief says 'Give me aman on ten people' (using 'ala'), the chief gets the right to choose which ten because 'ala' grants him superiority. If he uses 'and' or 'then' (wa/thumma), the choice goes to the giver of aman.
The passage from al-Siyar al-Kabir illustrates the practical consequence.
4
Note the exception for 'ala' in sales
In the phrase 'I sold you this for a thousand', 'ala' can be metaphorically interpreted as 'with' (ba) due to the context of exchange. This shows that the default rule can be overridden by context.
The text mentions this as a metaphorical usage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل كلمة «على» للإلزام " وأصله لإفادة معنى التفوق والتعلّي، ولهذا فإنه لا يحمل عليه. بدل علي في قوله علي ألف. لو قال: «لفلان عليّ ألف يحمل على الدين بخلاف ما لو قال: «عندي» أو «معي» أو «قبلي»، وعلى هذا قال في 'السير الكبير' : إذا قال رأس الحصن: «آمنوني على عشرة من أهل الحصن ففعلنا فالعشرة سواه وخيار التعيين له ، ولو قال: «آمنوني وعشرة» أو «فعشرة » أو « ثم عشرة» ففعلنا، فكذلك ثبت الأمان له والعشرة سواه. وخيار التعيين للآمن، وقد تكون «على» بمعنى الباء مجازا حتى لو قال: بعتك هذا على ألف يكون «على» بمعنى الباء لقيام دلالة المعاوضة. (1) قوله: [للإلزام] أي: لإثبات لزوم ما قبلها على ما بعدها وهذا المعنى العرفي المستعمل في عامة الأحكام ماخوذ نقلاً أو تجوّزاً عن معناها اللغوي وهو التعلّي والتفوّق، كقولنا : «زيد على السرير» أو «علــى السطح»، ولَمّا كان اللازم على الشيء كأنه يعلوه ويركبه ويتعلّى ويغلب عليه وكأنه فــــوق نفــــســه لوجوبه على ذمّة كان الإلزام كأنه معناها، كذا قيل. (2) قوله: [معنى التفوق والتعلي... آه] وهو أي: التعلّي قد يكون حسا كما في قولهم: «زيـــد علـــى السطح»، وقد يكون معنى كما في قولهم: «فلان علينا أمير» و «لفلان على دين»؛ لأنّ الدين يستعلى من يلزمه، ولذا يقال: ركبه» ،«دين كذا في "الفصول". (3) قوله : فالعشرة سواه... آه] أي: سوى رأس الحصن وهذا ليس بمقصود بالتفريع بل المقصود، وقوله: «وخيار التعيين له» أي لرأس الحصن؛ لأنه طلب أمان نفسه على عشرة بكلمة «على» الدالّــــة علـــــى التعلّى والتفوّق، فيقتضي أن يكون مستعلياً عليهم في ثبوت الأمان، وكذلك بأن يكون ولاية التعيين له حيث يختار من يشاء ويذر من يشاء، كذا في "المعدن". (4) قوله: [له] :أي لرأس الحصن لأنه طلب أمان نفسه على عشرة بكلمة «على»، فيكون مستعلياً عليهم في ثبوت الأمان، وذلك بأن يكون له عليهم ولاية التعيين حيث يختار من يشاء ويذر من يشاء. (5) قوله: [للأمن] لأنّ رأس الحصن عطف أمانهم على أمان نفسه من غير أن يشترط تعلياً عليهم في أمانهم، فلا يكون له الخيار أي لرأس ،الحصن، كذا في "المعدن".
Section: The word 'ala' is for obligation. And its origin is to convey the meaning of superiority and elevation. For this reason, it is not interpreted otherwise. In his saying 'ala alif', it replaces 'ala'. If he says 'so-and-so has against me a thousand', it is interpreted as a debt, unlike if he says 'indee' (with me) or 'ma'ee' (with me) or 'qablee' (in my possession). And upon this, it is said in al-Siyar al-Kabir: If the chief of the fort says: 'Give me aman (safe-conduct) on [the condition of] ten people from the fort, and we did, then the ten are other than him and the choice of designation is his.' And if he says: 'Give me aman and ten people' or 'then ten people' or 'then ten people', and we did, then similarly aman is established for him and the ten are other than him. And the choice of designation is for the one giving aman. And 'ala' can be metaphorically in the sense of 'ba' (with), such that if he says: 'I sold you this for a thousand', 'ala' is in the sense of 'ba' because of the indication of exchange. (1) His saying: 'for obligation' means: to establish the necessity of what is before it upon what is after it. This is the customary meaning used in most rulings, taken by transmission or metaphor from its linguistic meaning of elevation and superiority, like our saying: 'Zaid is on the bed' or 'on the roof'. Since what is obligatory upon something is as if it overcomes and rides it and dominates it, and it is above itself due to its obligation on the liability, obligation is as if its meaning, as is said. (2) His saying: 'the meaning of superiority and elevation...' meaning: elevation may be physical as in 'Zaid is on the roof', or abstract as in 'so-and-so is over us as an amir' and 'so-and-so has a debt upon him'; because debt overcomes the one obligated by it, and therefore it is said 'debt rides him', as in al-Fusul. (3) His saying: 'the ten are other than him...' meaning: other than the chief of the fort, and this is not the intended goal of the branching but the intended is his saying: 'and the choice of designation is his' i.e., for the chief of the fort; because he asked for aman for himself on the condition of ten with the word 'ala' which indicates elevation and superiority, so it requires that he be superior to them in the establishment of aman, and likewise that he have authority of designation, choosing whom he wishes and leaving whom he wishes, as in al-Ma'dan. (4) His saying: 'his' means for the chief of the fort, because he asked for aman for himself on ten with the word 'ala', so he is superior to them in the establishment of aman, and that is that he has authority over them to designate, choosing whom he wishes and leaving whom he wishes. (5) His saying: 'for the one giving aman' because the chief of the fort linked their aman to his own aman without stipulating superiority over them in their aman, so he does not have the choice, i.e., the chief of the fort, as in al-Ma'dan.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage defines the linguistic and legal usage of the word 'على' (ala). In legal contexts, its primary meaning is obligation (الإلزام), derived from its literal meaning of superiority and elevation. When a person says 'for so-and-so upon me a thousand' (لفلان عليّ ألف), it is understood as a debt owed. However, if one says 'with me' (عندي) or 'with me' (معي) or 'in my possession' (قبلي), it does not imply obligation but mere possession. The text then applies this to aman (safe-conduct) in the context of war. If the chief of a fort says 'Give me aman on ten people from the fort' (آمنوني على عشرة من أهل الحصن), using 'على', the aman is established for the chief, and the ten are separate; the chief has the right to choose which ten. If he uses 'and' (وعشرة) or 'then' (فعشرة) or 'then' (ثم عشرة), the aman is still for him and the ten are separate, but the choice of designation belongs to the one giving aman (the Muslims), not the chief. This is because 'على' gave him superiority. The text also notes that 'على' can be used metaphorically to mean 'باء' (with) in the context of exchange, e.g., 'I sold you this for a thousand' where 'على' means 'with'. The footnotes elaborate on the etymology and application in al-Siyar al-Kabir and al-Ma'dan.

Key Terms
على (ala): Preposition indicating obligation and superiority.
إلزام (ilzam): Making something necessary upon someone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the word 'على' indicate in the phrase 'لفلان عليّ ألف'?
A) A debt owed by the speaker
B) Possession of a thousand by the speaker
C) A gift from the speaker
D) Ambiguous meaning

Key Takeaway
The word 'على' in legal usage indicates obligation and superiority, which affects who has the right to designate in aman contracts.

The Particle 'في' in Oaths: Location and Time Rulings
Explains how the particle 'في' affects oath fulfillment in location and time contexts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule for interpreting the particle 'في' in conditional oaths to determine when an oath is broken.

Core Idea
For location oaths, verb transitivity determines whose location matters—agent for intransitive, object for transitive.

In Hanafi fiqh, the precise interpretation of the particle 'في' in oaths depends on the type of verb. Imam Muhammad's examples from al-Jami' al-Kabir illustrate this nuanced rule. Understanding this principle is crucial for correctly determining the fulfillment of oaths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the verb type
Determine whether the verb in the oath is intransitive (e.g., insult) or transitive (e.g., strike, kill). The verb category dictates which entity is considered the 'container' (zarf).
Intransitive verbs require only the agent to complete the action.
2
Apply location rule for intransitive verbs
For intransitive verbs, the oath is fulfilled if the agent (the one performing the action) is present in the specified location at the time of the action.
Example: Swearing 'If I insult you in the mosque' – the oath is broken if the insulter is in the mosque, regardless of the insulted person's location.
3
Apply location rule for transitive verbs
For transitive verbs, the oath is conditional on the object (the one receiving the action) being in the specified location. The agent's location is irrelevant.
Example: 'If I strike you in the mosque' – the oath is broken only if the person struck is inside the mosque.
4
Handle time-based oaths
For actions that take time (e.g., killing), the oath is broken only if the entire action is completed within the specified time frame. The moment of completion (e.g., death) determines the time.
Wounding before Thursday but dying on Thursday breaks the oath; wounding on Thursday but dying on Friday does not.
5
Exclude prior acts
Oaths only apply to future actions. If part of the action occurred before the oath, it is not considered part of the conditional. The oath only covers subsequent events.
If a fatal wound was inflicted before the oath, the subsequent death does not break the oath even if it occurs during the specified time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل كلمة في للظرف
يتحقق بأثره وأثره في المحل. قال محمد رحمه الله في "الجامع الكبير": إذا قال: «إن ستمتك في المسجد فكذا» فشتمه وهو في المسجد والمشتوم خارج المسجد يحنث ولو كان الشاتم خارج المسجد والمشتوم في المسجد لا يحنث، ولو قال: «إن ضربتك» أو «شججتك في المسجد فكذا يشترط كون المضروب والمشجوج في المسجد ولا يشترط كون الضارب والشاج فيه، ولو قال: «إن قتلتك في يوم الخميس فكذا فجرحه قبل يوم الخميس ومات يوم الخميس يحنث ولو جرحه يوم الخميس ومات يوم الجمعة لا يحنث.
(1) قوله: [ وأثره في المحلّ] أي: في محلّ يقع عليه فيراعي المكان والزمان في حق المحلّ، كذا في "المعدن".
(۲) قوله : [ يحنث] لأنّ الشتم يتمّ بالشاتم وحده فكان شرط الحنث وجوده في المسجد وقد وجد، كذا قيل.
(۳) قوله: [لا يحنث] وهذا مشكل؛ لأنّ تحققه كما يكون بما يؤثر فيه يكون بالمؤثر أيضاً، فكلاهما مما يتوقف عليه الفعل واشتراط الظرفية في أحدهما دون الآخر تحكّم؛ لأنا نقول : لَمّا كان الفعل متعـ متعدياً وذكر المحلّ مع الفاعل يكون المقصود ووقوع الفاعل على المحلّ ضرورةً ويكون المحل هو المقصود فاشتراط الظرفية في المحلّ لهذا، كما في "مفتاح العلوم".
(٤) قوله: [يحنث] أي: الحالف المتكلّم بوجود الشرط وهو القتل في يوم الخميس؛ لأنّ القتل إنما يصير قتلاً عند زهوق الروح ألا ترى أنه قبل زهوق الروح في يوم الخميس يسمّى جرحاً وبعد زهــــوق الــــروح يسمّى قتلاً، فيراعى زمان زهوق الروح و لم يوجد زهوق الروح في يوم الخميس فلم يوجــــد شــرط الحنث وهو القتل فيه كذا قيل.
(٥) قوله ومات يوم الجمعة فإن قيل: لو كان ضربه يوم الأربعاء، ثُمّ حلف الخميس إن قتلتك يوم الجمعة فعبدي حرّ، فمات المضروب يوم الجمعة لا يحنث وإن وجد زهوق الروح في الجمعة، قلنا: إن الإيمان إنما شرعت للامتناع عن الفعل في المستقبل وليس في وسع الحالف الامتناع عن وقوع الفعل المحلوف عليه قبل عقد اليمين فلا يكون التعليق السابق على الحلف داخلاً في اليمين فلذا لا يحنث، كذا في بعض الحواشي.
Section: The word 'fi' for container. It is realized by its effect and its effect in the place. Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said in al-Jami' al-Kabir: If he says, 'If I insult you in the mosque, then such-and-such,' and he insults him while he is in the mosque and the one insulted is outside the mosque, he is guilty of breaking the oath. But if the insulter is outside the mosque and the one insulted is in the mosque, he is not guilty. And if he says, 'If I strike you' or 'If I wound your head in the mosque, then such-and-such,' it is conditional that the one struck and the one wounded be in the mosque, and it is not conditional that the striker and the wounder be in it. And if he says, 'If I kill you on Thursday, then such-and-such,' and he wounds him before Thursday and he dies on Thursday, he is guilty; but if he wounds him on Thursday and he dies on Friday, he is not guilty.
(1) His saying: 'and its effect in the place' means in the place on which it falls, so place and time are considered with respect to the place, as in al-Ma'dan.
(2) His saying: 'he is guilty' because the insult is completed by the insulter alone, so the condition of guilt is his presence in the mosque, and it has occurred, as is said.
(3) His saying: 'he is not guilty' is problematic; because its realization is both by what affects it and by the one affecting it, so both are necessary for the action, and conditioning the container in one without the other is arbitrary. For we say: Since the verb is transitive and the mention of the place with the agent indicates that the object is intended and the agent's occurrence on the object is necessary, and the place is the object, so conditioning the containericity in the object is for this reason, as in Miftah al-Ulum.
(4) His saying: 'he is guilty' means the oath-taker, due to the existence of the condition which is killing on Thursday; because killing only becomes killing when the soul departs. Do you not see that before the soul departs on Thursday it is called wounding, and after the soul departs it is called killing. So the time of the soul's departure is considered, and the soul's departure has not occurred on Thursday, so the condition of guilt (killing on Thursday) has not occurred, as is said.
(5) His saying: 'and he dies on Friday' — if it is said: if he struck him on Wednesday, then swore on Thursday 'If I kill you on Friday, then my slave is free,' and the struck one dies on Friday, he is not guilty even though the soul's departure occurred on Friday. We say: Oaths are legislated to prevent an action in the future, and it is not within the power of the oath-taker to prevent the occurrence of the action sworn about before the oath, so the prior suspension is not included in the oath, hence he is not guilty, as in some commentaries.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is an usul rule explaining how the particle 'في' (in) functions in conditional oaths, specifically regarding location and time. The discussion is based on examples from Imam Muhammad's al-Jami' al-Kabir, which is a core text of the Zahir al-Riwayah. The key principle: for intransitive verbs (like insulting), the oath is fulfilled by the agent's presence in the specified location; for transitive verbs (like striking), the object's presence is the condition. For time-based oaths, the completion of the action (e.g., death) at the specified time determines guilt. The commentary elaborates on the rationale, noting that the linguistic analysis of the verb type determines which element (agent or object) is considered the container. A special case arises when the action (killing) spans multiple days; the oath is only broken if the entire action (death) occurs within the specified time. The footnote about previous actions being excluded from oaths clarifies that oaths only affect future actions, not past ones.

Key Terms
في (fi): A particle indicating location or time within which an action occurs, or used conditionally.
ظرف (zarf): A container—either locative or temporal—that encompasses the action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person swears: 'If I hit my son in the yard, my wife is divorced.' The father hits his son while the father is in the yard and the son is inside the house. According to the Hanafi rule, is the oath broken?
A) Yes, because the father was in the yard.
B) No, because the son was not in the yard.
C) Yes, because hitting occurred.
D) No, because the oath is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule for 'في' in oaths hinges on verb transitivity: intransitive verbs consider the agent's location, transitive verbs consider the object's location, and for time, the completion moment governs.

The Usul of Divorce Oaths: Distinguishing Mashiyya and Ilm
Differentiating between divine will and knowledge in divorce oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle to differentiate between 'في مشيئة الله' and 'في علم الله' in divorce oaths and derive the correct ruling for each.

Core Idea
في مشيئة الله suspends divorce; في علم الله makes it immediate because divine knowledge entails existence.

In Hanafi usul, the meaning of a word can change the ruling. The passage from al-Shashi examines two seemingly similar divorce oaths: one suspended on God's will, the other on God's knowledge. While both use the particle 'في', the ruling differs because of the underlying theological distinction between will and knowledge. This lesson will guide you through the linguistic and rational analysis that leads to the Hanafi conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrases
The husband uses 'في مشيئة الله' or 'في علم الله'. Note that the particle 'في' here indicates a location, but with divine attributes it takes on a different function.
2
Analyze 'في مشيئة الله'
This is treated like 'إن شاء الله' (if Allah wills). Since God's will is not necessarily realized, the divorce becomes conditional on an uncertain event, so she is not divorced.
The condition is the existence of God's will, which we cannot know, so divorce does not occur.
3
Analyze 'في علم الله'
The usul scholars interpret 'ilm' here as 'ma'lum' (the known). Because God's knowledge is always real and certain, 'في علم الله' means 'in what God knows', which is necessarily existent. Therefore, divorce occurs immediately upon utterance.
Key distinction: knowledge necessitates existence; will does not.
4
Derive the ruling
Apply the principle: 'al-ilm bi al-wujud wa al-mashiyya bi al-tawaquf' (knowledge entails existence, will entails waiting). Thus, for 'في علم الله', the talaq is binding immediately; for 'في مشيئة الله', it is suspended.
This shows how usul principles connect theological concepts to fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أصول الشاشي مع أحسن الحواشي
فصل كلمة في للظرف
كتاب للإمام محمد رحمه الله. ١٢
قال: أنت طالق في مشيئة الله تعالى أو في إرادة الله تعالى كان ذلك بمعنى الشرط حتى لا تطلق .
أن لعدم إدراك وجود الشرط. ۱۲
من الغد؛
(۱) قوله: [ حين تجيء من الغد] يعني: إذا حلف وقت الزوال يقع الطلاق إذا جاء وقت الزوال لأن الشرط معنى يوم كامل، فإذا مضي نصف النهار في يوم الحلف والنصف الثاني من الغد كان اليوم كاملاً فوقع الطلاق لوجود الشرط، كذا في "المعدن". ١٢
(۲) قوله : [لو قال أنت طالق ... إلخ] لأنّه لو قال: «أنت طالق إن شاء الله تعالى» كان ذلك إبطال قولــــه: أنت طالق فكذا ما كان بمعناه، فإن قلت: قوله : «أنت طالق في علم الله» يقع به الطلاق في الحال مع العلم مثل الإرادة في كونهما لا يصلحان ظرفاً؛ لأنهما فعلان قيل إنّ العلم يستعمل بمعنى المعلوم، يقال: «اللهم اغفر علمك فينا أي معلومك، ويقال: «علم أبي حنيفة أي: معلومه، وإذا كان بمعـــــى المعلوم يستحيل أن يجعل بمعنى الشرط؛ لأنّ الشرط ما يكون على خطر الوجود ومعلـوم الله تعالى متحقق لا محالة، وإذا كان كذلك كان الطلاق واقعاً في الحال؛ لأنه جعل معلوم الله تعالى ظرفاً للطلاق وإنما يكون الطلاق في معلومه إذا كان واقعاً؛ لأنه لو لم يكن واقعاً لكان عدمه في معلومه بخــــلاف المشية؛ لأنّ مشيئة الله تعالى ليست متحققة حتماً أي وجوباً، وتحقيقه أنّ الله تعالى يوصف بالمشيئة وبضدّها ولا يوصف بضدّ العلم فكان العلم متحققاً لا محالة والمشيئة لا يلزم أن تكون موجودة حتماً، كذا في "الفصول"، قلت : الأظهر مما قالوا في جواب الاعتراض بقوله : فإن قلت:... إلخ» أن يقال إنه لا حاجة إلى جعل العلم بمعنى العلوم، بل المراد أنه ثابت في علم الله تعالى بمعنى: أن علمه محيط بذلك أي: ما ذكره في "التلويح" إلا أنّ الشارح نقل جواب الأصوليين مع جعل العلم بمعنى المعلوم لورود الاعتراضات على جوابهم بالإرادة والقدرة ليعلم الفرق بين العلم والإرادة والقدرة لوقوع الطلاق في العلم دون الإرادة والقدرة، فافهم. ١٢
Principles of al-Shashi with the best footnotes: Chapter on the word 'fi' for location. Book of Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him). He said: 'You are divorced in the will of Allah Almighty or in the desire of Allah Almighty' that is in the meaning of condition, so she is not divorced. For lack of perceiving the existence of the condition. From the next day. (1) [When it comes from the next day] meaning: if he swore at noon, divorce occurs when noon comes because the condition is the meaning of a full day. So if half of the day passed in the day of the oath and the second half from the next day, the day is complete, so divorce occurs due to existence of the condition. (2) [If he said 'You are divorced...' etc.] Because if he said: 'You are divorced if Allah wills', that nullifies his statement 'You are divorced', and similarly what is in its meaning. If you said: His statement 'You are divorced in the knowledge of Allah' results in divorce immediately, yet knowledge is like will in that both are not suitable as location because they are actions. It is said that knowledge is used in the sense of the known. They say: 'O Allah, forgive Your knowledge in us' meaning Your known, and it is said: 'the knowledge of Abu Hanifa' meaning his known. And when it is in the sense of the known, it is impossible to make it mean condition, because condition is something whose existence is uncertain, while what is known by Allah is necessarily realized. If so, divorce occurs immediately because he made the known of Allah a location for divorce, and divorce is in His known only if it occurs; if it were not occurring, its non-occurrence would be in His known, unlike will, because the will of Allah is not necessarily realized. The verification: Allah is described by will and its opposite, but not by the opposite of knowledge, so knowledge is necessarily realized while will is not necessarily existing. I say: The most apparent from what they said in answering the objection is that there is no need to make knowledge in the sense of the known; rather, the intention is that it is established in the knowledge of Allah in the sense that His knowledge encompasses it, as mentioned in al-Talwih. But the commentator transmitted the answer of the usul scholars with making knowledge in the sense of the known due to objections to their answer in terms of will and power, to show the difference between knowledge and will and power regarding the occurrence of divorce in knowledge but not in will and power, so understand.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of 'في' in divorce oaths, focusing on cases involving divine attributes. When a husband says 'You are divorced in the will of Allah' or 'in the desire of Allah', the phrase is interpreted as a condition (shart) meaning 'if Allah wills', so divorce does not occur because the condition (His will) is unknown and not necessarily existent. However, when he says 'in the knowledge of Allah', the ruling differs. The footnote explains that 'knowledge' here is interpreted as 'the known' (al-ma'lum), meaning what is already determined in Allah's knowledge. Since Allah's knowledge is necessarily realized, making divorce dependent on it would imply that if divorce is in His knowledge, it must occur immediately. Thus, divorce occurs instantly upon utterance, unlike the case with will. The commentator reconciles different views, noting that some scholars argue that 'knowledge' should be taken literally, but the prevalent Hanafi position distinguishes between knowledge (which necessitates existence) and will (which does not). This analysis demonstrates the subtlety of Hanafi usul in treating linguistic particles with theological concepts.

Key Terms
مشيئة (mashiyya): Divine will; when used with 'في', it indicates condition and does not necessitate occurrence.
علم (ilm): Divine knowledge; here interpreted as 'known' (ma'lum), which is necessarily existent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main reason why 'في علم الله' causes immediate divorce while 'في مشيئة الله' does not?
A) Because 'ilm' is a stronger attribute than 'mashiyya'.
B) Because 'ilm' is reinterpreted as 'ma'lum' which is necessarily existent, while 'mashiyya' is not necessarily existent.
C) Because the wife must agree to divorce in the case of 'mashiyya' but not for 'ilm'.
D) Because the husband must intend immediate divorce for 'ilm' to work.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, 'في علم الله' in a divorce oath causes immediate divorce because 'ilm' is interpreted as 'ma'lum', the necessarily existent known of Allah.

Conditional Pronouncements and Future Ownership
Explaining the validity of conditional divorce and manumission when the condition is future ownership.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on conditional divorce and manumission with future ownership and evaluate the Shafi'i critique of its validity.

Core Idea
A conditional pronouncement takes effect only when its condition is fulfilled; the object need not exist at utterance.

This passage addresses a key usul dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i concerning the validity of conditional divorce and manumission when the condition involves future ownership. At issue is whether the pronouncement must be attached to a valid object at the time of utterance or only when the condition occurs. The Hanafi school holds that the pronouncement becomes a cause upon fulfillment of the condition, while the Shafi'i school requires the cause to be effective immediately.

Guided Path
1
State the dispute and the scenario
Identify the exact scenarios: saying to a stranger woman 'If I marry you, you are divorced' and to someone else's slave 'If I own you, you are free.' Understand which school considers this valid and why.
Shafi'i: invalid; Hanafi: valid if attributed to ownership or its cause.
2
Analyze the Shafi'i position and its proof
Explain why Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the pronouncement is invalid: the 'cause' must be established at the time of utterance, and the object (mahall) is not owned, so the cause is null.
Al-Shafi'i analogizes to selling a free person or a dead animal.
3
Analyze the Hanafi position and its proof
Explain the Hanafi reasoning: the pronouncement is not a cause at utterance but becomes a cause when the condition occurs. Thus, the object need only exist at that later time. They require attribution to ownership or a cause of ownership to ensure the object will exist.
The Hanafi position is supported by the principle that the 'illa' is not required at the start.
4
Apply the principle to derived rulings
The same usul difference underlies two other rulings: (1) maintenance for an irrevocably divorced woman (mubattata) – Shafi'i only if pregnant (based on Quran 65:6); Hanafi allows from other evidence. (2) Ability to marry a free woman prevents marrying a slave woman – Shafi'i (based on Quran 4:25); Hanafi allows if no ability. Note the common thread: Shafi'i treats absence of condition as a preventer; Hanafi does not.
These rulings illustrate the broader impact of the usul principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل وأما بيان التغيير فيما إذا قال لأجنبية: «إن تزوّجتك فأنت طالق» أو قال لعبد الغير: «إن ملكتك فأنت حر» يكون التعليق باطلا عنده؛ لأن حكم التعليق انعقاد صدر الكلام علة والطلاق والعتاق ههنا لم ينعقد علة لعدم إضافته إلى المحل المذكور. فبطل حكم التعليق فلا يصح التعليق، وعندنا كان التعليق صحيحا حتى إذا تزوجها يقع الطلاق؛ لأن كلامه إنما ينعقد علة عند وجود الشرط والملك لوجود الشرط وهو التزوج ثابت عند وجود الشرط فيصحّ التعليق، ولهذا المعنى قلنا: شرط صحة التعليق للوقوع في صورة عدم الملك أن يكون مضافا إلى الملك أو إلى سبب الملك حتى لو قال لأجنبية: «إن دخلت الدار فأنت طالق» ثم تزوجها ووجد الشرط لا يقع الطلاق لعدم الإضافة إلى الملك أو سببه. وكذلك طول الحرّة يمنع جواز نكاح الأمة عنده؛ لأن الكتاب علق نكاح الأمة بعدم الطول فعند وجود الطول كان الشرط عدما وعدم الشرط مانع من الحكم فلا يجوز، وكذلك قال الشافعي رحمه الله: «لا نفقة للمبتوتة إلا إذا كانت حاملا»؛ لأن الكتاب علق الإنفاق بالحمل لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِن كُنَّ أُولات حَمْلٍ فَأَنفِقُوا عَلَيْهِنَّ حَتَّى يَضَعْنَ حَمْلَهُنَّ﴾ فعند عدم الحمل كان الشرط عدما وعدم الشرط مانع من الحكم عنده، وعندنا لما لم يكن عدم الشرط مانعا من الحكم جاز أن يثبت الملك.
(1) قوله: [انعقاد صدر الكلام علّة...] ولقائل أن يقول: لفظ «صدر الكلام» إنما يستقيم فيما إذا أخر الشرط بأن قال: «إن تزوجتك مثلاً»، وأما إن قدم الشرط بأن قال: «إن تزوجتك فأنت طالق» فلا يمكن أن يجاب عنه بأنّ الجزاء مقدّم حكماً؛ لأنّ المقصود هو الجزاء والشرط قيد له، ولذلك قالوا: المعتبر في الجملة الشرطية هو الجزاء، فالجزاء إن كان خبراً فالجملة خبرية، نحو: إن جئتني أكرمك، وإن كان إنشاء فالجملة إنشائية نحو: إن جاء زيد فأكرمه.
(2) قوله: [إلى المحل] فإنّ المحل شرط حال صيرورة إيجاب الطلاق والعتاق سبباً بالإجماع ولم يوجد والسبب إذا أضيف إلى غير محله بطل كالبيع إذا أضيف إلى الحرّ والدم والأجنبية مثلاً.
(3) قوله: [ولهذا المعنى...] هذه المسئلة فرعية هذا الأصل المختلف: أي: عندنا لما لم يكن المعلّق سبباً قبل وجود الشرط لم يكن المحل شرطاً لصحة التعليق، لكنه لما كان تعريفه أن يصير سبباً عند وجود الشرط شرطنا أن يكون التعليق بالملك أو سبب الملك كالهبة والتزويج وإنّما شرطنا ذلك أي: إضافة المعلّق إلى الملك أو سببه ليوجد المحلّ عند صيرورته أي: الإيجاب علة فيصح كونه سبباً.
(4) قوله: [قلنا شرط...] هذه المسئلة عندنا متفرّعة على هذا الأصل المختلف فيه بيننا وبينه وإنمـا شرطنا ذلك أي: إضافة المعلّق إلى الملك أو إلى سببه ليوجد المحلّ عند صيرورة الإيجاب علـة فــيــصـح كونه سببا وعلة.
(5) قوله: [لا يقع الطلاق] لعدم وجود الشرط وهو أن يكون التعليق مضافاً إلى الملك أو إلى سببه بل التعليق في المثال المذكور مضافا إلى دار.
(6) قوله: [و كذلك...] أي: مثل ما يتصوّر يتفرّع المسألة السابقة على الأصل المختلف يتفرع مسئلة طول الحرّة أي: القدرة على نكاح الحرّة.
(7) قوله: [لأنّ الكتاب...] حيث قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَمَن لَّمْ يَسْتَطِعْ مِنكُمْ طَوْلاً أَن يَنكِحَ الْمُحْصَنَاتِ الْمُؤْمِنَاتِ فَمن ما مَلَكَتْ أَيْمَانُكُم مِّن فَتَيَاتِكُمُ الْمُؤْمِنَاتِ﴾ أي: من لم يقدر منكم على نكاح الحرائر فلينكح من الإماء المسلمات.
(8) قوله: [من الحكم إلى زمان وجود الشرط فالطول مانع من جواز نكاح الأمة فلا يجوز نكاح الأمــــة عند طول الحرّة عنده وعندنا لَمّا لم يكن عدم الشرط مانعاً من الحكم كان عدم الحكم قبل الشرط بالعدم الأصلي فلم يكن هذا النص أي نص التعليق نافياً لجواز نكاح الأمة بدون الشرط وغاية أنه لا يثبت هذا الحكم بهذا النصّ فجاز أن يثبت بدليل آخر من النص أو غيره.
(9) قوله: [جاز...] قلت: تفرّع هذا الخلاف على الاختلاف في الأصل المذكور في حيز الخفاء؛ لأنّ التعليق عنده مانع للحكم قبل وجود الشرط ومانع عن السبب عندنا ومنع وجود السبب منـــع لوجـــــود الحكم؛ لأن الحكم يوجد بوجود سببه.
Chapter on the explanation of alteration: when a man says to a stranger woman: 'If I marry you, you are divorced' or says to someone else's slave: 'If I own you, you are free', the conditional pronouncement is invalid according to him (al-Shafi'i) because the effect of conditional pronouncement is that the beginning of the speech becomes a cause, and divorce and manumission here do not become a cause because they are not attributed to the mentioned locus. Thus the effect of conditional pronouncement is nullified, so the conditional pronouncement is not valid. According to us (Hanafis), the conditional pronouncement is valid, such that when he marries her, the divorce occurs; because his speech only becomes a cause at the occurrence of the condition, and ownership exists at the occurrence of the condition (which is marriage), so the conditional pronouncement is valid. For this meaning we said: the condition for the validity of a conditional pronouncement for occurrence in a case where ownership is absent is that it be attributed to ownership or to a cause of ownership. So if he says to a stranger woman: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced,' then marries her and the condition occurs, the divorce does not occur due to lack of attribution to ownership or its cause. Similarly, the ability (to marry a free woman) prevents the permissibility of marrying a slave woman according to him (al-Shafi'i) because the Book (Quran) conditions the permissibility of marrying a slave woman on the absence of ability; when ability exists, the condition is absent, and absence of the condition prevents the ruling, so it is not permissible. Similarly, al-Shafi'i said: 'No maintenance for the irrevocably divorced woman unless she is pregnant' because the Book conditions maintenance on pregnancy in His saying: {And if they are pregnant, then spend on them until they give birth}. So when pregnancy is absent, the condition is absent, and absence of the condition prevents the ruling according to him. According to us, since absence of condition does not prevent the ruling, ownership may be established (by another evidence).
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This is a usul dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the validity of conditional pronouncements (ta'liq) when the condition involves future ownership. Al-Shafi'i holds that conditional divorce or manumission uttered to someone not owned at the time of utterance is invalid because the pronouncement is not attached to a valid object (mahall). According to him, the pronouncement must be a cause at the moment of utterance to be effective; since the object is not owned, the cause is null. The Hanafis argue that the pronouncement is not a cause at the moment of utterance but becomes a cause at the moment the condition occurs. Thus, the object (mahall) is only required at that later moment. For validity, the Hanafis require that the conditional pronouncement be attributed to ownership or to a cause of ownership (such as marriage or gift). For example, saying to a stranger woman 'If I marry you, you are divorced' is valid because marriage is a cause of ownership, so when marriage occurs, the object is present. However, saying 'If you enter the house, you are divorced' to a stranger woman is invalid because it is not attributed to ownership or its cause, so even if he later marries her and she enters the house, the divorce does not occur. The commentary expands on this principle, noting that the same usul difference underlies two other rulings: (1) the ability to marry a free woman prevents marrying a slave woman according to al-Shafi'i, based on Quran 4:25, which conditions permissibility on the lack of ability; the Hanafis hold that the absence of the condition does not prevent the ruling from being established by another evidence (such as general permissibility). (2) Maintenance for an irrevocably divorced woman (mubattata) is only due if she is pregnant according to al-Shafi'i, based on Quran 65:6, which mentions spending only for pregnant women; the Hanafis again allow maintenance from another source. The author explains that these disputes stem from the same usul principle: whether the absence of a condition is a preventing factor for the ruling or not.

Key Terms
تعليق (ta'liq): A conditional pronouncement where a legal effect (divorce, manumission) is made contingent on a future event.
علة (illa): The cause or effective reason for a legal ruling; in conditional pronouncements, the speech becomes a cause at the moment of condition fulfillment.
محل (mahall): The locus or object of the pronouncement, which must exist (be owned) at the time the cause becomes effective.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis in this passage, if a man says to a stranger woman 'If I marry you, you are divorced,' and later marries her, what happens?
A) The divorce is invalid because she was not his wife at the time of the pronouncement.
B) The divorce occurs upon marriage because the pronouncement is attributed to a cause of ownership (marriage).
C) The divorce occurs immediately upon the pronouncement because it is a valid conditional divorce.
D) The pronouncement is suspended until he owns her, but it never takes effect because he never owned her at the time of utterance.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a conditional pronouncement becomes a cause upon fulfillment of the condition, so the object need only be owned at that later time, not at the moment of utterance.

Shubha from Textual Evidence: Hadd and Lineage
Derivation of hadd and lineage rulings from shubha based on hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of shubha from a textual evidence (dalil naqli) to determine whether a hadd punishment applies and to distinguish when such shubha also establishes lineage.

Core Idea
A textual shubha can prevent hadd but does not automatically establish lineage.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi demonstrates how a single hadith can create a legal doubt (shubha) that affects the application of punishments and lineage rulings. The derivation is a classic example of istinbat, showing how a general text (zahir) is interpreted in light of consensus and other evidence. We will walk through the chain of reasoning from the hadith to the ruling, and see why the same shubha suffices for dropping the hadd but not for confirming lineage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source text and its apparent meaning
Identify the hadith 'You and your property belong to your father' and note that the lam in 'li-abik' indicates ownership. The apparent meaning (zahir) is that the father has a right of possession over the son's property.
This is a dalil naqli, a transmitted textual evidence.
2
Classify the text in Hanafi usul
Determine the textual category: this is a zahir (apparent) text. It does not explicitly assert ownership as a fact (nass), but implies it strongly.
Hanafi usul: zahir is a category that indicates a meaning with some probability, but may be subject to specification (takhsis) or interpretation.
3
Apply the governing usul principle
Apply the principle that shubha arising from a textual evidence (even if not fully operative due to consensus) is sufficient to prevent hadd. The hadith's implication of ownership creates a doubt that blocks the punishment.
The shubha is effective regardless of the son's belief (whether he thought it halal or haram), because the factor is the evidence, not his opinion.
4
Derive the ruling for hadd
Derive: if the son thought intercourse was permissible (i.e., he relied on the shubha), the hadd is dropped. If he thought it was forbidden, the hadd applies because he had no valid doubt.
This shows the usul principle that shubha is considered an objective legal factor, not subjective.
5
Distinguish the case of lineage
Note that the same shubha does not establish lineage because lineage requires actual ownership or a valid marriage contract. The shubha only affects the punishment, not the substantive status of the child.
The distinction is based on the different legal consequences: hadd is dropped on doubt, but lineage requires certainty or a recognized cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل الواجب على المجتهد أي الأب. ومالك لأبيك فسقط إعتبار ظنه في الحل والحرمة في ذلك ولو وطئ الابن أي مملوكته. الابن الواطي. الابن الواطي جارية أبيه. أي جارية أبيه. جارية أبيه يعتبر ظنّه في الحل والحرمة حتى لو قال: «ظننت أنها علي حرام» يجب الحد، ولو قال: ظننت أنها علي حلال» لا يجب الحد؛ لأنّ شبهة الملك في مال الأب لم يثبت له بالنص فاعتبر رأيه ولا يثبت نسب الولد وإن ادعاه. (1) قوله: [لأبيك] فإنّ اللام للملك، فظاهر الحديث يدلّ على أنّ للأب حق التملك في مال ولده إلاّ أنّ حقيقة ثبوت الملك له ساقط بالإجماع وبالنصوص فتصير شبهة دائرة وإن ظنّ الحرمة؛ لأنّ المؤثر في الإسقاط هو الدليل الشرعي وذلك لا يتفاوت بين معتقد الحل والحرمة، كذا في "المعدن". (2) قوله: [لا يجب الحد ولا يرد عليه ما لو وطئ جارية أخيه أو أخته، وقال: «إنّي ظننت أنّها تحلّ لي». فإنه لم يجعل الجهل فيه شبهة في سقوط الحد؛ لأنّ منافع الأملاك بينهما متبائنة عادةً، فلا يكون هذا محل الاشتباه فلا يصير شبهةً. (3) قوله: [ولا يثبت نسب الولد... إلخ] لأنّ الفعل تمحض زنا في نفسه، لكن بحكم الاشتباه يسقط الحدّ وهذا الاشتباه لا يوجب ثبات النسب؛ لأنّ ثبوته يعتمد قيام الملك في المحلّ من وجه أو قيام المحلّ فيه ولم يوجد بخلاف الشبهة في المحل؛ لأنها نشأت عن دليل شرعي وهو قوله عليه السلام: «أنت ومالك لأبيك» وهو قائم فلا يفرق الحال بين الظنّ وعدمه في سقوط الحد.
Chapter on the duty of the mujtahid: meaning the father. And ‘You and your property belong to your father’ so his opinion regarding permissibility and prohibition falls away in that matter. And if the son has intercourse with his father’s slave-girl, his opinion regarding permissibility and prohibition is considered: if he says ‘I thought it was forbidden to me,’ the hadd is obligatory; if he says ‘I thought it was permissible for me,’ the hadd is not obligatory because of the shubha of ownership over the father’s property, which is not established for him by textual evidence, so his opinion is considered. And the lineage of the child is not established even if he claims it. (1) His statement: [for your father] – indeed the lam indicates ownership, so the apparent meaning of the hadith indicates that the father has a right to possess his son’s property, but the reality of ownership is negated by consensus and by texts, so it becomes a shubha that is effective even if he thought it forbidden; because the effective factor in dropping (the hadd) is the legal evidence, and that does not differ between belief in permissibility or prohibition, as in al-Ma‘din. (2) His statement: [The hadd is not obligatory] – and the objection is not raised that if he had intercourse with his brother’s or sister’s slave-girl and said ‘I thought it was permissible for me,’ ignorance is not considered a shubha for dropping the hadd because the benefits of ownership between them are normally distinct, so this is not a place of confusion, thus it does not become a shubha. (3) His statement: [And the lineage of the child is not established... etc.] – because the act is pure fornication in itself, but due to confusion the hadd is dropped; this confusion does not necessitate the establishment of lineage because its establishment depends on the existence of ownership in the place from one aspect or the existence of the place in it, and that does not exist, unlike the shubha in the place (ownership) because it arose from a legal evidence, namely his statement (peace be upon him) ‘You and your property belong to your father,’ which stands, so the situation does not differ between having an opinion (of permissibility) or not regarding the dropping of the hadd.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the hadd punishment and lineage when a son has intercourse with his father's slave-girl. The key proof is the hadith 'You and your property belong to your father,' which creates a shubha (legal doubt) regarding ownership. Because of this shubha, if the son honestly thought intercourse was forbidden, the hadd applies; if he thought it was permissible, the hadd is dropped due to the doubt. However, this shubha does not establish lineage because actual ownership is lacking. The footnotes clarify: the shubha arises from the hadith's implication of the father's right to possess, even though full ownership is not established by consensus; the shubha is effective regardless of the son's belief. Additionally, the case is distinguished from that of a brother's or sister's slave-girl, where no shubha applies because ownership spheres are normally separate.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubha): A doubt arising from a legal evidence that prevents the application of a hadd punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a son having intercourse with his father's slave-girl, why is the hadd punishment not applied when the son says he thought it was permissible?
A) Because the son owns the father's property.
B) Because of a shubha from the hadith 'You and your property belong to your father'.
C) Because the father consented.
D) Because the son is not a free person.

Key Takeaway
A textual shubha can prevent hadd but does not automatically establish lineage; the effect of a textual evidence is determined by its legal implications, not subjective belief.

The Principle of Sabab: Attribution of Rulings to Apparent Causes
Usul rule defining sabab as substitute for hidden ‘illa with application to witness liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a ruling is attached to its sabab (apparent cause) when the true 'illa is hidden, and identify how this principle determines liability in cases of witness testimony and attestation.

Core Idea
When the true cause is hidden, rulings attach to the apparent cause (sabab) to remove hardship.

In Usul al-Shashi, the rule 'al-hukm yata'allaqu bi-sababihi' is introduced as a foundational principle of Hanafi legal theory. This passage explains that when the effective cause ('illa) of a ruling is not directly accessible, the Lawgiver attaches the ruling to a manifest attribute (sabab) that typically accompanies the hidden cause. The author illustrates this with the case of a witness whose testimony leads to property loss: even though the judge's ruling seems directly responsible, the witness is held liable because the judge is considered compelled—like an animal driven by its owner. This lesson unpacks the definition of sabab, its proof by qiyas, and a related intra-Hanafi dispute on attestation (tazkiya).

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
Read the opening line: 'al-hukmu yata'allaqu bi-sababihi.' This is the core usul rule. The ruling is attached to its cause. Identify that 'sabab' here means the apparent cause that substitutes for the hidden effective cause ('illa).
The passage later explains that sabab is established when the true 'illa is unknown, to ease the obligation upon the mukallaf.
2
Examine the example of witness liability
The author gives the case: a witness testifies, property is lost due to that testimony, then the witness retracts. The loss is attributed to the witness (he is liable), not the judge. Understand why: the judge is compelled to rule on the testimony of upright witnesses; his act is considered involuntary in the legal view.
The text compares the judge to a blind man led by a guide (al-a'ma bi-yad al-qa'id).
3
Analyze the qiyas analogy
The proof for attributing the loss to the witness is a qiyas: just as the movement of an animal is causally attributed to its driver (because it goes when he drives and stops when he stops), so the judge's ruling is attributed to the witness's testimony. Work through the analogy: the judge is like the animal (passive/compelled), the witness is like the driver.
This qiyas is stated explicitly: 'because the movement of the animal is attributed by causality to the driver.'
4
Differentiate the dispute on tazkiya
The passage notes a difference of opinion between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn) regarding attestors (muzakkun) who retract their attestation of a witness's uprightness. Abu Hanifa holds them liable; the Sahibayn do not. Trace the reasoning: Abu Hanifa considers retraction as revealing falsehood, so the attestors are like false witnesses; the Sahibayn argue that praise (thana') is not a cause of loss, and the judge is free in his ruling based on that praise.
This illustrates how the sabab concept is applied analogically: does attestation function as a sabab similar to testimony?

فصل الحكم يتعلق بسببه. الشاهد. ۱۲ أي الشهادة. ١٢ إذا أتلف بشهادته مالا فظهر بطلانها بالرجوع ضمن؛ لأن سير الدابة يضاف بالعلية. ١٢ (1) أي القاضي. ١٢ أي القاضي. ١٢ إلى السوق وقضاء القاضي يضاف إلى الشهادة لما أنه لا يسعه ترك القضاء أي القاضي. ١٢ أي العاجز. ١٢ القضاء فيضاف التلف إلى الشاهد. ١٢ بعد ظهور الحق بشهادة العدل عنده فصار كالمجبور في ذلك بمنزلة البهيمة كالأعمى بيد القائد. ١٢ القاضي. مجبورة. ١٢ المفضي الذي لا يضاف إليه الوجوب. ١٢ بفعل السائق، ثم السبب قد يقام مقام العلة عند تعذر الإطلاع على حقيقة العلة تيسيرا للأمر على المكلّف ويسقط به اعتبار العلة ويدار الحكم على الظاهر. ١٢ القاضي كالبهيمة محمول على القضاء بعد إقامة البينة كذا في 'الفصول'. ١٢ (۱) قوله: [يضاف إلى السوق] لأنّ الدابة تسير على طبع السائق، ولهذا تقف بإيقافه وتسير بسيره، فصار مضافاً إلى السائق، كذا في 'المعدن'. ١٢ (۲) قوله: [بعد ظهور الحق... إلخ] فيه إيماء إلى أن فعل القضاء من القاضي وإن كان فعلاً اختيارياً صادراً من العبد المختار باختياره، فكان ينبغي أن يضاف حكم ضمان المال بضياعه إلى فعل القضاء ولم يضمنه الشهود لما أن شهادتهم سبب محض كما في الدلالة إلا أنّ القاضي لما اعتبر عند الشارع عاجزاً مجبوراً من حيث لا يسعه على مقتضى الشرع غير القضاء على حسب شهادة المشهود بعد تعديلـهـم وتزكيتهم عدّ فعله بهذا النظر فعلا غير اختياري في الملاحظة الشرعية وصار حكمه حكم فعل البهيمة في عدم صلوح إضافة الحكم إليه هذا البيان في الشهادة، وأما في التزكية فإذا رجع المزكون عن التزكية فعند الإمام الأعظم رحمه الله يضمنان المال بهذا الوجه، وعندهما لا فافهم اثنوا على مسلم والثناء ليس سبباً للتلف وليست علته إلا قضاء القاضى وهو مختار في قضاء على أنّ رجوعهم لا يستلزم كـــذاب الشهود، فلا يضاف التلف إلى رجوعهم عن التزكية ، أصله كذا في 'الحصول'. ١٢ (۳) قوله: [ على السبب ] لما أنّ في التكليف يعني على العمل بحقيقة العلة من الحرج، فلذا سقط اعتبار العلة. ١٢
Section: The ruling is attached to its cause. The witness — meaning the testimony. If one causes loss of property through his testimony and then its invalidity becomes apparent by retraction, he is liable, because the movement of an animal is attributed by causality to the driver. (1) Meaning the judge. The judge's judgment is attributed to the testimony because he cannot leave off judging after truth appears through the testimony of a just witness before him, so he becomes like one compelled in that, like an animal, like a blind man led by a guide. The judge is like an animal compelled; the facilitator to whom obligation is not attributed. Then the cause (sabab) may be established in place of the effective cause ('illa) when it is impossible to know the true effective cause, to make things easy for the obligated person, and thereby consideration of the effective cause falls away, and the ruling is made to turn on the apparent. The judge is like an animal carried on the judiciary after establishing proof, as in 'al-Fusul'. (1) His saying: 'attributed to the market' because the animal moves by the nature of the driver, so it stops when he stops and goes when he goes, thus it is attributed to the driver, as in 'al-Ma'din'. (2) His saying: 'after truth appears...' it contains an indication that the act of judging by the judge, although it is a voluntary act issuing from a free agent by his choice, so it would have been appropriate to attribute the liability for loss of property to the act of judging and not hold the witnesses liable because their testimony is a pure cause, as in brokerage, except that the judge — since he is considered by the Lawgiver as incapable and compelled, in that he cannot but judge according to the testimony of witnesses after they are declared upright and trustworthy — his act is considered by this view as involuntary in the legal consideration, and his ruling becomes like the act of an animal in not being suitable for attribution of the ruling. This statement applies to testimony. As for tazkiyah (attesting to uprightness), if the attestors retract their attestation, according to Imam al-A'zam (may Allah have mercy on him) they are liable for the property in this manner, but according to the two companions they are not. So understand: they praised a Muslim; praise is not a cause for loss, and its effective cause is only the judge's ruling, and he is free in his ruling, and their retraction does not necessitate that the witnesses are liars, so loss is not attributed to their retraction from attestation. The origin is in 'al-Husul'. (3) His saying: 'to the cause' because in obligation there is difficulty if acting on the true effective cause, so consideration of the effective cause falls away.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi introduces the principle that a ruling is attached to its cause (sabab), and when the true effective cause ('illa) is hidden, the apparent cause is treated as the effective cause for legal purposes. The author illustrates this with the case of witness liability: if a witness gives testimony that leads to loss of property, and later retracts, the loss is attributed to the testimony (the sabab) rather than to the judge's ruling, because the judge is compelled to rule based on the testimony of upright witnesses. The commentary in Ahsan al-Hawashi elaborates that the judge's act is considered involuntary in the legal view, similar to an animal's movement being attributed to its driver. The passage also notes a difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions regarding the liability of those who attest to a witness's uprightness (muzakkun) if they retract.

Key Terms
السبب (al-sabab): The apparent cause that is established in place of the effective cause ('illa) when the latter is hidden, to facilitate rulings.
العلة (al-'illa): The effective cause or ratio legis that actually necessitates the ruling, but may be hidden.
المجبور (al-majbur): One who is compelled, here the judge whose ruling is considered involuntary because he must judge by the testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the witness liable for property loss when his testimony is retracted, rather than the judge?
A) Because the judge acted intentionally and voluntarily.
B) Because the witness's testimony is the true effective cause ('illa).
C) Because the judge is considered compelled and his ruling is attributed to the testimony (sabab).
D) Because the judge is not a free agent in Islamic law.

Key Takeaway
The ruling is attached to its sabab (apparent cause) when the true effective cause is hidden; the witness becomes the cause of loss because the judge is compelled.

The Quality of the Cause Determines the Quality of the Ruling
Explaining how the completeness/deficiency of temporal causes affects the obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that the ruling mirrors its cause (al-hukm yatba' al-sabab) to determine whether an obligation is performed completely or deficiently, and explain the Hanafi position on multiple causes for a single effect.

Core Idea
The cause's completeness determines the ruling's completeness; a deficient cause yields a deficient obligation.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi explores a foundational Hanafi principle: the legal ruling is attached to its cause, and the quality (completeness or deficiency) of the cause directly affects the quality of the obligation. Using Fajr and Asr prayers as case studies, the text explains why sunrise nullifies Fajr (because the cause was complete but becomes deficient) while Asr performed at the time of sunset redness is valid but deficient (because the cause was always deficient). The commentator also addresses a deeper theoretical issue: how multiple time segments can each be a cause for a single obligation without causing multiplicity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
Recognize the statement: الأحكام الشرعية تتعلق بأسبابها – legal rulings are attached to their causes. The quality of the hukm depends on the quality of its sabab.
This is a cardinal Hanafi usul rule, later expressed as al-hukm yaduru ma'a 'illatihi wujudan wa 'adaman.
2
Apply to Fajr prayer
The cause of Fajr is the time before sunrise, which is complete (kamil). If the sun rises during prayer, the remaining time is deficient (naqis, makruh). Since the ruling was established with completeness, performing it with deficiency would change its quality, so it is nullified (batala).
The nullification is because performance with a deficient cause cannot fulfill an obligation established with a complete cause.
3
Apply to Asr prayer
The cause of Asr at the end time (sunset redness) is inherently deficient (time is disliked, attributed to Satan). Therefore the obligation is established with deficiency from the start. Performing it then is valid but deficient (sahih naqis), and no repetition is required.
This is a concession due to necessity (darura) and general hardship (umum balwa).
4
Examine the theoretical question
If every part of the time is a cause for the same obligation, would that multiply obligations? The commentator presents two solutions: (a) causality transfers (intiqal) from the first part to the next, or (b) multiple causes concur (taraduf) to produce a single effect. The Hanafi school accepts both but favors taraduf.
The text defends taraduf using analogies: multiple nullifiers of wudu, multiple witnesses for a single ruling, etc.
5
Understand the evidence for taraduf
The commentator cites fiqh examples where multiple independent causes produce the same effect: urine, blood, and cupping each independently nullify wudu; two witnesses each establish the same claim; reciting each verse of a long Quranic passage fulfills the duty of recitation. This refutes the objection that multiple causes cannot have one effect.
This is a distinctive Hanafi position; other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may reject multiple independent causes for a single effect.

Chapter: The legal rulings are attached to their causes. Incomplete. 12 Chapter: The legal rulings are attached to their causes because it is attributed to Satan. 12 i.e., sunrise. 12 The dawn is complete, but the time becomes corrupt only with sunrise, and that after the exit of any worship you performed for them. 12 The time then the obligation is established with the description of completeness. So if the sun rises during the prayer, the obligation is nullified; because he cannot complete the prayer except with the description of deficiency, considering he starts anew at the time of redness, then it becomes obligatory deficiently. 12 (4) The time, and if that part is deficient as in the Asr prayer, then the end of the time i.e., time of Asr. 12 i.e., redness of the sun. 12 i.e., the obligation is established. 12 The time of redness of the sun, and the time according to him is corrupt, so the duty is established with the description of deficiency. The legal acts are carried on ugliness and corruption, and it is established in Hanafi principles that the prohibition of something not for its essence but is an affirmation of legality and validity, and they gave the example of fasting on the day of Nahr, and prayer in the disliked time, so nothing is necessitated except sin, not corruption, so ponder. Thus in 'al-Husul'. 12 (1) His saying: [with the description of completeness] because of the completeness of its cause; because the end of Fajr time is not described with dislike, and what is established as complete is not performed with the description of deficiency, thus it is said. 12 (2) His saying: [the obligation is nullified] and it may be said: it should not be nullified by sunrise; because the cause is the part connected to the commencement, which is a complete time, and the remaining parts of the time are mere containers, and deficiency of the container does not affect the deficiency of the contained. That may be answered with reflection, thus said some. 12 (3) His saying: [except with description... etc.] because deficiency of performance is due to deficiency of what it is performed in, which is time, and this time is deficient, disliked among the times of idol worshipers, so performance is corrupted, and its obligation was complete due to the completeness of its cause, which is the part connected to the performance as well, even if the cause exists but the container condition is corrupted, resulting in corruption of the conditioned. This is a minor corruption from the aspect of the cause, not from the aspect of the strong condition, so this type of corruption is necessary, and it is possible in Asr due to the deficiency of its obligation and due to necessity and general affliction and other factors at that time, so ponder, thus in 'al-Husul'. 12 No (4) His saying: [as in Asr prayer] i.e., if that part is deficient as in Asr prayer, he starts anew at the time of redness, then it becomes obligatory deficiently; because its cause, which is the part connected to performance, is corrupt and deficient as it is attributed to Satan, as mentioned in the well-known hadith. So the duty is established, i.e., established according to the establishment of its cause, so it is performed with the description of deficiency. For this reason, it was necessary to say the permissibility of Asr time in the disliked time despite the corruption of the time, thus in 'al-Fusul'. 12 Assembly: 'al-Madinah al-Ilmiyyah' (Islamic Call) (276) [PAGE_285] Usul al-Shashi with Ahsan al-Hawashi Chapter: The legal rulings are attached to their causes i.e., the duty is established with the description of deficiency. 12 i.e., permissibility of Asr. 12 i.e., redness of the sun. 12 i.e., its dislike. 12 from consideration of causality. 12 For this reason, it was necessary to say permissibility according to him despite the corruption of the time. The second way is to make i.e., transfer of causality from the first part to the second. 12 Every part of the time a cause not through transfer, then saying it means every part is a cause not through transfer. 12 Nullifying the causality established by law, and this does not necessitate multiplication of the obligation, because i.e., the second part establishes the same as what the first part established. 12 The second part only establishes the same as what the first part established, so this is from the chapter of concurrence or oath on his saying, so the cause of the obligation of prayer at the beginning of the section. 12 Of causes and multitude of witnesses in the chapter of litigation, and the cause of the obligation of fasting is witnessing i.e., Ramadan. 12 (4) The month for directing address upon witnessing the month, and addition of fasting to it, and i.e., the month. 12 (1) His saying: [nullifying causality... etc.] because if the first part becomes a cause legally, it effects the obligation itself, so if it is said that causality transfers from it, then it is an invalid causality, and this is not permissible. The excuse from those who said: the first way is the establishment of a quality in a place after its establishment in another place, and this is not transfer but resembles transfer, so it is called transfer metaphorically, thus in 'al-Fusul'. 12 (2) His saying: [and this does not necessitate... etc.] Repelling an objection raised against this way, that if every part of the time is a cause, then each part should have an obligation, thereby multiplying obligations, which is not the case. He answered: the causes are multiple while the obligation is one, so multiplication does not follow, because the second part establishes only when the first part does not establish, thus in 'al-Ma'din'. 12 (3) His saying: [and multitude of witnesses... etc.] This indicates repelling what appears of the impossibility of a single effect with multiple causes, based on the famous notion that independent causes concurring on a single individual effect is impossible, whether simultaneously or consecutively by consensus, or in an alternative manner according to the chosen view of the verifiers. He repelled it by saying that this has been permitted by jurists, as in the concurrence of causes, like when multiple causes come together for a single ruling, such as when one urinates, has a nosebleed, and gets cupped, the ruling is attributed to each of them, and as narrated similarly from Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him), and as they said regarding the meaning of wadi breaking wudu despite following urine, and breaking what is broken is impossible, and as in multitude of witnesses, the ruling is attributed to every two of them, or to each individual in what one witness suffices like sighting the crescent of Ramadan, and as in a long recitation, the ruling of obligation of fasting or performing the duty is attributed to each seer or to each verse, thus in 'al-Husul'. 12 (4) His saying: [and addition of fasting to it etc.] It is said: fasting of the month of Ramadan; because the principle in addition of a thing is that the second term is the cause of the first and its occurrence; because addition is for specification, and the principle in everything established is completeness, and completeness.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a chapter heading from Usul al-Shashi concerning how legal rulings (ahkam) are connected to their causes (asbab). The commentator explains two related issues: (1) the effect of sunrise on Fajr prayer, and (2) the nature of causality across time segments. The core Hanafi principle stated is that the quality of the cause (sabab) determines the quality of the ruling (hukm). For Fajr, the cause is the time before sunrise, which is complete (kamil). If sunrise occurs during prayer, the remaining time is deficient (naqis) because it is disliked (makruh) due to its association with sun worship. Therefore, the prayer cannot be completed in a complete manner; it becomes null (batala) and must be made up later. However, for Asr prayer, the end time (redness of sunset) is inherently deficient, so if one prays then, the obligation is fulfilled with deficiency, and it is valid despite the dislike. The commentary then delves into a theoretical discussion: how can multiple parts of a time each be a cause for the same obligation without causing multiplicity? Two ways are proposed: either causality transfers from one part to the next (intiqal), or each part is independently a cause but the later establishes the same obligation as the earlier (taraduf al-‘ilal). The latter is defended with analogies from fiqh: multiple causes (e.g., urine, blood, sleep) can each independently nullify wudu, or multiple witnesses can each independently establish a ruling. The Hanafi position is that multiple causes can produce a single effect if they are alternative rather than cumulative. This is a subtle usul point distinguishing Hanafi from some other schools who reject multiple independent causes for one effect.

Key Terms
السبب (al-sabab): That which necessitates the ruling; the legal cause that triggers an obligation.
الفاسد (al-fasid): Corrupt or invalid; a time that is legally deficient due to dislike or prohibition.
ترادف العلل (taraduf al-‘ilal): Concurrence of causes; multiple independent causes producing the same effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if the sun rises while one is performing Fajr prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) The prayer is valid and complete.
B) The prayer becomes null and must be made up later.
C) The prayer is valid but deficient.
D) One must stop and continue after sunrise.

Key Takeaway
The quality of the hukm mirrors the quality of its sabab; a complete cause requires complete performance, while a deficient cause may permit a deficient but valid performance, and multiple causes can concur for a single ruling (taraduf al-‘ilal).

The Causes (Asbab) of Zakat, Hajj, and Sadaqat al-Fitr in Hanafi Usul
Defining the causes of three acts of worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the cause (sabab) for each of zakat, hajj, and sadaqat al-fitr as stated in the text, and distinguish each from its condition (shart).

Core Idea
The cause of zakat is productive nisab; of hajj is the House; of sadaqat al-fitr is the dependent person.

This passage from al-Shashi's Usul introduces the fundamental principle that Shariah rulings are attached to their causes. It then specifies the causes for three obligatory acts. Understanding the distinction between cause and condition is crucial for correct application, especially regarding early payment.

Guided Path
1
Locate the general principle
The text begins with a فصل stating that rulings are attached to their causes. Note this axiom.
2
Identify the cause for zakat
Extract the phrase: 'سبب وجوب الزكاة ملك النصاب النامي'. Understand that the nisab must be productive (real or notional).
The commentary clarifies that 'productive' includes both actual growth through trade and notional growth via the passing of a year.
3
Analyze the condition for zakat
The passage of a year (hawl) is identified as a condition, not the cause, as clarified in the commentary. How does early payment become permissible?
The hadith of al-Abbas permits early payment, confirming the cause alone triggers obligation.
4
Identify the cause for hajj
The text states: 'سبب وجوب الحج البيت'. Note that ability (istita'a) is a condition.
5
Identify the cause for sadaqat al-fitr
The text states: 'سبب وجوب صدقة الفطر رأس يمونه' (the head of the dependent). The day of fitr is a condition, not the cause.
The commentary addresses the objection that a person (rā's) cannot be an effective cause because it is an essence, not a description.
